<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_the_Jacksonville_area" title="List of companies based in the Jacksonville area">List of companies based in the Jacksonville area</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CSXJAX15.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/CSXJAX15.JPG/220px-CSXJAX15.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/CSXJAX15.JPG/330px-CSXJAX15.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/CSXJAX15.JPG/440px-CSXJAX15.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CSXJAX15.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation_Building" title="CSX Transportation Building">CSX Transportation Building</a> serves as headquarters for <a href="/wiki/CSX_Corporation" title="CSX Corporation">CSX Corporation</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Jacksonville's location on the <a href="/wiki/St._Johns_River" title="St. Johns River">St. Johns River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> proved providential in the growth of the city and its industry. Jacksonville has a sizable deepwater port, which helps make it a leading port in the U.S. for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">automobile</a> imports, as well as the leading <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transportation" title="Transportation">transportation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Distribution_(business)" title="Distribution (business)">distribution</a> hub in the state. However, the strength of the city's economy lies in its broad diversification. While the area once had many thriving dairies such as <a href="/wiki/Gustafson%27s_Farm" title="Gustafson's Farm">Gustafson's Farm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skinner_Dairy" title="Skinner Dairy">Skinner Dairy</a>, this aspect of the economy has declined over time. The area's economy is balanced among <a href="/wiki/Distribution_(business)" title="Distribution (business)">distribution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biomedical_technology" title="Biomedical technology">biomedical technology</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consumer_goods" title="Consumer goods">consumer goods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Information" title="Information">information</a> services, <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">insurance</a> and other industries.</p>
<p>Jacksonville is home to many prominent corporations and organizations, including the headquarters of four <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> companies: <a href="/wiki/CSX_Corporation" title="CSX Corporation">CSX Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fidelity_National_Financial" title="Fidelity National Financial">Fidelity National Financial</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fidelity_National_Information_Services" title="Fidelity National Information Services">Fidelity National Information Services</a> and <a href="/wiki/BI-LO_(United_States)" title="BI-LO (United States)">Southeastern Grocers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Interline_Brands" title="Interline Brands">Interline Brands</a> is based in Jacksonville and is currently owned by <a href="/wiki/The_Home_Depot" title="The Home Depot">The Home Depot</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Florida_East_Coast_Railway" title="Florida East Coast Railway">Florida East Coast Railway</a>, Swisher International, Inc., and the large short line railroad holding company <a href="/wiki/RailAmerica" title="RailAmerica">RailAmerica</a> are also based in Jacksonville.</p>
<p>In 2008, Jacksonville had approximately 2.8 million visitors who stayed overnight, spending nearly $1 billion. Research Data Services of Tampa was commissioned to undertake the study, which quantified the importance of tourism. The total economic impact was $1.6 billion and supported nearly 43,000 jobs, 10% of the local workforce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Banking_and_financial_services">Banking and financial services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Banking and financial services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LaurastBOAT.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2526" data-file-width="1895" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/LaurastBOAT.jpg/220px-LaurastBOAT.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/LaurastBOAT.jpg/330px-LaurastBOAT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/LaurastBOAT.jpg/440px-LaurastBOAT.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LaurastBOAT.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Tower_(Jacksonville)" title="Bank of America Tower (Jacksonville)">Bank of America Tower</a> located on <a href="/wiki/Laura_Street" title="Laura Street">Laura Street</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Jacksonville has long had a regional legacy in banking and finance. Locally headquartered <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_National_Bank" title="Atlantic National Bank">Atlantic National Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida_National_Bank" title="Florida National Bank">Florida National Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barnett_Bank" title="Barnett Bank">Barnett Bank</a> dominated the industry in Florida from the turn of the 20th century through the 1980s, before all being acquired in a national wave of mergers and acquisitions throughout the entire financial sector. Acquired by <a href="/wiki/NationsBank" title="NationsBank">NationsBank</a> in 1997, Barnett Bank was the last of these banks to circum to acquisition, and at the time was the largest banking merger in U.S. history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> The city still holds distinction nationally and internationally, boosting two Fortune 500 financial services companies, <a href="/wiki/Fidelity_National_Financial" title="Fidelity National Financial">Fidelity National Financial</a> and <a href="/wiki/FIS_(company)" title="FIS (company)">FIS</a>, FIS being well recognized as a global leader in <a href="/wiki/Financial_technology" title="Financial technology">financial technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> Headquartered on the banks of the St. Johns River in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Jacksonville" title="Downtown Jacksonville">Downtown Jacksonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/EverBank" title="EverBank">EverBank</a> holds the title of largest bank in the state by deposits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> The city is home to other notable financial services institutions including <a href="/wiki/Ameris_Bancorp" title="Ameris Bancorp">Ameris Bancorp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Financial" title="Atlantic Coast Financial">Atlantic Coast Financial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Knight_Financial_Services" title="Black Knight Financial Services">Black Knight Financial Services</a>, <a href="/wiki/MedMal_Direct_Insurance_Company" title="MedMal Direct Insurance Company">MedMal Direct Insurance Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/US_Assure" title="US Assure">US Assure</a>, and <a href="/wiki/VyStar_Credit_Union" title="VyStar Credit Union">VyStar Credit Union</a>. The city is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_Bank_of_Atlanta_Jacksonville_Branch" title="Federal Reserve Bank of Atlanta Jacksonville Branch">Federal Reserve Bank of Atlanta Jacksonville Branch</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jacksonville's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_sector" title="Financial sector">financial sector</a> has benefited from a rapidly changing business culture, as have other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunbelt" title="Sunbelt">Sunbelt</a> cities like <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tampa" title="Tampa">Tampa</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charlotte" title="Charlotte">Charlotte</a>. In a concept known as <a href="/wiki/Nearshoring" title="Nearshoring">nearshoring</a>, financial intuitions are shifting operations away from high-cost addresses like <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a>, and have even shifted trading functions to Jacksonville.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> With relatively low-cost real estate, easy access to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, high-quality of life and 19,000 financial sector employees, Jacksonville has become an appealing option for relocating staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> Perhaps the best example of this is the growth of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a>'s presence in the city. Jacksonville is home to Deutsche Bank's second largest US operation, only New York is larger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> Other institutions with a notable presence in Jacksonville include <a href="/wiki/Macquarie_Group" title="Macquarie Group">Macquarie Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a>, <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citi" title="Citi">Citi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citizens_Property_Insurance" title="Citizens Property Insurance">Citizens Property Insurance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fidelity_Investments" title="Fidelity Investments">Fidelity Investments</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ally_Financial" title="Ally Financial">Ally Financial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aetna" title="Aetna">Aetna</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logistics">Logistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Logistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CMA_CGM_Virginia_-_IMO_9351139_(3194444689).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1406" data-file-width="2100" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/CMA_CGM_Virginia_-_IMO_9351139_%283194444689%29.jpg/220px-CMA_CGM_Virginia_-_IMO_9351139_%283194444689%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/CMA_CGM_Virginia_-_IMO_9351139_%283194444689%29.jpg/330px-CMA_CGM_Virginia_-_IMO_9351139_%283194444689%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/CMA_CGM_Virginia_-_IMO_9351139_%283194444689%29.jpg/440px-CMA_CGM_Virginia_-_IMO_9351139_%283194444689%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CMA_CGM_Virginia_-_IMO_9351139_(3194444689).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Container_ship" title="Container ship">Container ship</a> at <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Jacksonville" title="Port of Jacksonville">Port of Jacksonville</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Jacksonville is a <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">rail</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air" title="Air">air</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">highway</a> focal point and a busy port of entry, with <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_International_Airport" title="Jacksonville International Airport">Jacksonville International Airport</a>, ship repair <a href="/wiki/Shipyard" title="Shipyard">yards</a> and extensive freight-handling facilities. <a href="/wiki/Lumber" title="Lumber">Lumber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paper" title="Paper">paper</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cigars" title="Cigars">cigars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pulp_(paper)" title="Pulp (paper)">wood pulp</a> are the principal exports; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobiles" title="Automobiles">automobiles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> are among imports. The city's <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a> base provides just 4.5% of local jobs, versus 8.5% nationally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> According to Forbes in 2007, Jacksonville, Florida ranked 3rd in the top ten U.S. cities to relocate to find a job.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> Jacksonville was also the 10th fastest growing city in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>To emphasize the city's transportation business and capabilities, the Jacksonville Regional Chamber of Commerce filed <i>Jacksonville America's Logistics Center</i> as a trademark on November 9, 2007. It was formally registered on August 4, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> Cornerstone began promoting the city as "Jacksonville: America's Logistics Center" in 2009. Signs were added to the existing city limit markers on Interstate 95.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Jacksonville" title="Port of Jacksonville">Port of Jacksonville</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seaport" title="Seaport">seaport</a> on the <a href="/wiki/St._Johns_River" title="St. Johns River">St. Johns River</a>, is a large component of the local economy. Approximately 50,000 jobs in Northeast Florida are related to port activity and the port has an economic impact of $2.7 billion in Northeast Florida:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cecil_Commerce_Center" title="Cecil Commerce Center">Cecil Commerce Center</a> is located on the site of the former Naval Air Station Cecil Field which closed in 1999 following the 1993 <a href="/wiki/Base_Realignment_and_Closure" title="Base Realignment and Closure">Base Realignment and Closure</a> (BRAC) decision. Covering a total area of 22,939 acres (92.83 km<sup>2</sup>), it was the largest military base in the Jacksonville area. The parcel contains more than 3% of the total land area in Duval County (17,000 acres (69 km<sup>2</sup>)). The industrial and commercial-zoned center offers mid to large-size parcels for development and boasts excellent transportation and utility infrastructure as well as the third-longest runway in Florida.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_technology">Media and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Media and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Media in Jacksonville, Florida">Media in Jacksonville, Florida</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ftuhq.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1673" data-file-width="2232" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ftuhq.jpeg/220px-Ftuhq.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ftuhq.jpeg/330px-Ftuhq.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ftuhq.jpeg/440px-Ftuhq.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ftuhq.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/The_Florida_Times-Union" title="The Florida Times-Union">The Florida Times-Union</a></i> Building</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Florida_Times-Union" title="The Florida Times-Union">The Florida Times-Union</a></i> is the major daily newspaper in Jacksonville and the First Coast. Jacksonville.com is its official website. The <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_News_%26_Daily_Record" title="Financial News &amp; Daily Record">Financial News &amp; Daily Record</a></i> is a daily paper focused on the business and legal communities. Weekly papers include the <i><a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Business_Journal" title="Jacksonville Business Journal">Jacksonville Business Journal</a></i>, an <a href="/wiki/American_City_Business_Journals" title="American City Business Journals">American City Business Journals</a> publication focused on business news, <i><a href="/wiki/Folio_Weekly" title="Folio Weekly">Folio Weekly</a></i>, the city's chief <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alternative_weekly" title="Alternative weekly">alternative weekly</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Florida_Star" title="The Florida Star">The Florida Star</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Free_Press" title="Jacksonville Free Press">Jacksonville Free Press</a></i>, two weeklies catering to African Americans. <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jax4Kids&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jax4Kids (page does not exist)">Jax4Kids</a></i>, a monthly newspaper, caters to parents. <a class="external text" href="http://www.Jax4Kids.com/" rel="nofollow">Jax4Kids.com</a> is its official website. <i><a href="/wiki/EU_Jacksonville" title="EU Jacksonville">EU Jacksonville</a></i> is a monthly entertainment magazine. <a href="/wiki/Metro_Jacksonville" title="Metro Jacksonville">Metro Jacksonville</a> is an online-only publication.</p>
<p>Jacksonville is the 47th largest local television market in the United States,.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> Despite its large population, Jacksonville has always been a medium-sized market because the surrounding suburbs and rural areas are not much larger than the city itself. It is served by <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a> stations affiliated with major American networks including <a href="/wiki/WTLV" title="WTLV">WTLV</a> 12 (<a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>) and its sister station <a href="/wiki/WJXX" title="WJXX">WJXX</a> 25 (<a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>), <a href="/wiki/WJAX-TV" title="WJAX-TV">WJAX-TV</a> 47 (<a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a>) and <a href="/wiki/WFOX-TV" title="WFOX-TV">WFOX-TV</a> 30 (<a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a>; with <a href="/wiki/MyNetworkTV" title="MyNetworkTV">MyNetworkTV</a>/<a href="/wiki/MeTV" title="MeTV">MeTV</a> on DT2), which operates WJAX-TV under a <a href="/wiki/Local_marketing_agreement" title="Local marketing agreement">joint sales and shared services agreement</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WJCT_(TV)" title="WJCT (TV)">WJCT</a> 7 (<a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a>), and <a href="/wiki/WCWJ" title="WCWJ">WCWJ</a> 17 (<a href="/wiki/The_CW" title="The CW">CW</a>). <a href="/wiki/WJXT" title="WJXT">WJXT</a> 4, <a href="/wiki/WCWJ" title="WCWJ">WCWJ</a>'s sister station, is a former longtime <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> affiliate that turned independent in 2002.</p>
<p>Jacksonville is the 49th largest local radio market in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> and is dominated by the same two large ownership groups that dominate the radio industry across the United States: <a href="/wiki/Cox_Communications" title="Cox Communications">Cox Radio</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/IHeartMedia" title="IHeartMedia">iHeartMedia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> The dominant AM radio station in terms of ratings is <a href="/wiki/WOKV" title="WOKV">WOKV 690AM</a>, which is also the flagship station for the Jacksonville Jaguars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> In May 2013, WOKV began simulcasting on 104.5 FM as WOKV FM. There are two <a href="/wiki/Radio_broadcasting" title="Radio broadcasting">radio stations</a> broadcasting a primarily contemporary hits format; <a href="/wiki/WAPE-FM" title="WAPE-FM">WAPE 95.1</a> has dominated this niche for over twenty years, and more recently has been challenged by <a href="/wiki/WKSL" title="WKSL">WKSL</a> 97.9 FM (KISS FM). <a href="/wiki/WJBT" title="WJBT">WJBT</a> 93.3 (The Beat) is a <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip-hop</a>/<a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">R&amp;B</a> station, 96.9 The Eagle <a href="/wiki/WJGL" title="WJGL">WJGL</a> operates a Classic Hits format while its HD subchannel <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=WJGL-HD2&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="WJGL-HD2 (page does not exist)">WJGL-HD2</a> operates an Urban CHR format under the moniker Power 106.1, <a href="/wiki/WWJK" title="WWJK">WWJK 107.3</a> is an Adult Variety station. <a href="/wiki/WXXJ" title="WXXJ">WXXJ 102.9</a> is an alternative station, WQIK 99.1 is a <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country</a> station as well as WGNE-FM 99.9, WCRJ FM 88.1/<a href="/wiki/WSOS-FM" title="WSOS-FM">WSOS-FM</a> 94.1 (The Promise) is the main <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contemporary_Christian" title="Contemporary Christian">Contemporary Christian</a> music station operating since 1984,and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WJCT-FM" title="WJCT-FM">WJCT</a> 89.9 is the local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio">National Public Radio</a> affiliate. <a href="/wiki/WJKV" title="WJKV">WJKV</a> 90.9 FM is an <a href="/wiki/Educational_Media_Foundation" title="Educational Media Foundation">Educational Media Foundation</a> K-LOVE outlet. The NPR and PRX radio show, <a href="/wiki/State_of_the_Re:Union" title="State of the Re:Union">State of the Re:Union</a>, hosted by performance poet and playwright, <a href="/wiki/Al_Letson" title="Al Letson">Al Letson</a>, is headquartered and produced in Jacksonville.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_and_defense">Military and defense</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Military and defense">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_101207-N-6106P-001_Pilots_assigned_to_the_Vikings_of_Electronic_Attack_Squadron_(VAQ)_129,_based_at_Naval_Air_Station_Whidbey_Island,_pract.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1565" data-file-width="2700" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/US_Navy_101207-N-6106P-001_Pilots_assigned_to_the_Vikings_of_Electronic_Attack_Squadron_%28VAQ%29_129%2C_based_at_Naval_Air_Station_Whidbey_Island%2C_pract.jpg/220px-US_Navy_101207-N-6106P-001_Pilots_assigned_to_the_Vikings_of_Electronic_Attack_Squadron_%28VAQ%29_129%2C_based_at_Naval_Air_Station_Whidbey_Island%2C_pract.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/US_Navy_101207-N-6106P-001_Pilots_assigned_to_the_Vikings_of_Electronic_Attack_Squadron_%28VAQ%29_129%2C_based_at_Naval_Air_Station_Whidbey_Island%2C_pract.jpg/330px-US_Navy_101207-N-6106P-001_Pilots_assigned_to_the_Vikings_of_Electronic_Attack_Squadron_%28VAQ%29_129%2C_based_at_Naval_Air_Station_Whidbey_Island%2C_pract.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/US_Navy_101207-N-6106P-001_Pilots_assigned_to_the_Vikings_of_Electronic_Attack_Squadron_%28VAQ%29_129%2C_based_at_Naval_Air_Station_Whidbey_Island%2C_pract.jpg/440px-US_Navy_101207-N-6106P-001_Pilots_assigned_to_the_Vikings_of_Electronic_Attack_Squadron_%28VAQ%29_129%2C_based_at_Naval_Air_Station_Whidbey_Island%2C_pract.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_101207-N-6106P-001_Pilots_assigned_to_the_Vikings_of_Electronic_Attack_Squadron_(VAQ)_129,_based_at_Naval_Air_Station_Whidbey_Island,_pract.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Boeing_F/A-18E/F_Super_Hornet" title="Boeing F/A-18E/F Super Hornet">Boeing F/A-18E/F Super Hornet</a> at <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Jacksonville" title="Naval Air Station Jacksonville">Naval Air Station Jacksonville</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Jacksonville is home to three naval facilities, and with <a href="/wiki/Naval_Submarine_Base_Kings_Bay" title="Naval Submarine Base Kings Bay">Naval Submarine Base Kings Bay</a> nearby makes Jacksonville the third largest naval presence in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Port_of_Jacksonville_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Port_of_Jacksonville-15">[15]</a></sup> Only Norfolk, Virginia and San Diego, California are bigger. The military is by far the largest employer in Jacksonville and its total economic impact is approximately $6.1 billion annually. Several veterans service organizations are also headquartered in Jacksonville including <a href="/wiki/Wounded_Warrior_Project" title="Wounded Warrior Project">Wounded Warrior Project</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Jacksonville" title="Naval Air Station Jacksonville">Naval Air Station Jacksonville</a> is a military airport located 4 miles (6.4 km) south of the central business district. Approximately 23,000 civilian and active-duty personnel are employed on the base. There are 35 operational units/squadrons assigned there and support facilities include an airfield for pilot training, a maintenance depot capable of virtually any task, from changing a tire to intricate micro-electronics or total engine disassembly. Also on-site is a Naval Hospital, a Fleet Industrial Supply Center, a Navy Family Service Center, and recreational facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Bataan_arrives_at_Naval_Station_Mayport_121102-N-IC228-001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2136" data-file-width="3216" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/USS_Bataan_arrives_at_Naval_Station_Mayport_121102-N-IC228-001.jpg/220px-USS_Bataan_arrives_at_Naval_Station_Mayport_121102-N-IC228-001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/USS_Bataan_arrives_at_Naval_Station_Mayport_121102-N-IC228-001.jpg/330px-USS_Bataan_arrives_at_Naval_Station_Mayport_121102-N-IC228-001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/USS_Bataan_arrives_at_Naval_Station_Mayport_121102-N-IC228-001.jpg/440px-USS_Bataan_arrives_at_Naval_Station_Mayport_121102-N-IC228-001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Bataan_arrives_at_Naval_Station_Mayport_121102-N-IC228-001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Bataan_(LHD-5)" title="USS Bataan (LHD-5)">USS Bataan (LHD-5)</a> at <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Mayport" title="Naval Station Mayport">Naval Station Mayport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Mayport" title="Naval Station Mayport">Naval Station Mayport</a> is a Navy Ship Base that is the third largest fleet concentration area in the U.S. Mayport's operational composition is unique, with a busy harbor capable of accommodating 34 ships and an 8,000-foot (2,400 m) runway capable of handling any aircraft used by the Department of Defense. Until 2007, it was home to the <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_John_F._Kennedy_(CV-67)" title="USS John F. Kennedy (CV-67)">USS <i>John F. Kennedy</i></a>, which locals called "Big John". In January 2009, the Navy committed to stationing a nuclear-powered carrier at Mayport when the official <i>Record of Decision</i> was signed. The port will require approximately $500 million in facility enhancements to support the larger vessel, which would take several years to complete.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> The carrier was projected to arrive in 2019, however an amphibious group was sent before the carrier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Blount_Island_Command" title="Blount Island Command">Blount Island Command</a> is a Marine Corps Logistics Base whose mission is to support the Maritime Prepositioning Force (MPF) which provides for rapid deployment of personnel to link up with prepositioned equipment and supplies embarked aboard forward deployed Maritime Prepositioning Ships (MPS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_Jacksonville_(SSN-699)" title="USS Jacksonville (SSN-699)">USS <i>Jacksonville</i></a>, a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_propulsion" title="Nuclear propulsion">nuclear-powered</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_class_submarine" title="Los Angeles class submarine">Los Angeles class submarine</a>, is a U.S. Navy ship named for the city. The ship's nickname is <i>The Bold One</i> and <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a> is her home port.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/125th_Fighter_Wing" title="125th Fighter Wing">Florida Air National Guard</a> is based at <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_International_Airport" title="Jacksonville International Airport">Jacksonville International Airport</a>.</p>
<p>Coast Guard Sector Jacksonville is located on the St. Johns River next to Naval Station Mayport. Sector Jacksonville controls operations from Kings Bay, Ga. south to Cape Canaveral, Fla. The CGC Kingfisher, CGC Maria Bray, and CGC Hammer are stationed at the Sector. Station Mayport is co-located with Sector Jacksonville and includes 25-foot (7.6 m) Response Boats, and 47-foot (14 m) Motor Life Boats.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leisure_and_entertainment">Leisure and entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Leisure and entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_attractions_and_events_in_Jacksonville,_Florida" title="List of attractions and events in Jacksonville, Florida">List of attractions and events in Jacksonville, Florida</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gator_bowl_jacksonville_fl_1961.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="465" data-file-width="600" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8f/Gator_bowl_jacksonville_fl_1961.jpg/220px-Gator_bowl_jacksonville_fl_1961.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8f/Gator_bowl_jacksonville_fl_1961.jpg/330px-Gator_bowl_jacksonville_fl_1961.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8f/Gator_bowl_jacksonville_fl_1961.jpg/440px-Gator_bowl_jacksonville_fl_1961.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gator_bowl_jacksonville_fl_1961.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Gator_Bowl_Stadium" title="Gator Bowl Stadium">Gator Bowl Stadium</a>, now <a href="/wiki/EverBank_Field" title="EverBank Field">EverBank Field</a>, where the annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gator_Bowl" title="Gator Bowl">Gator Bowl</a> has taken place since 1946.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Throughout the year, many annual events of various types are held in Jacksonville. In sports, the annual <a href="/wiki/Gate_River_Run" title="Gate River Run">Gate River Run</a> has been held annually since March 1977.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> It has been the US National 15-kilometre (9.3 mi) <a href="/wiki/Road_running" title="Road running">road race</a> Championship since 1994 and is the largest race of its distance in the country with over 13,000 runners, spectators, and volunteers, making it Jacksonville's largest participation sporting event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSNBC_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC-147">[145]</a></sup> In college football, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gator_Bowl" title="Gator Bowl">Gator Bowl</a> is held on January 1. It has been continuously held since 1946. Also, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida%E2%80%93Georgia_game" title="Florida–Georgia game">Florida–Georgia game</a> (also known as the "World's Largest Outdoor Cocktail Party"), the annual <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> game between the rival <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_football" title="Florida Gators football">Florida Gators</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Bulldogs_football" title="Georgia Bulldogs football">Georgia Bulldogs</a> has been held in Jacksonville almost yearly since 1933. For six days in July the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Kingfish_Tournament" title="Jacksonville Kingfish Tournament">Jacksonville Kingfish Tournament</a> is held for fishermen of all skills. With $500,000 of prizes up for grabs, up to 1000 boats participate with almost 30,000 spectators watching. Jacksonville is also home of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_City_Pride" title="River City Pride">River City Pride</a> which is Northeast Florida's largest Gay Pride parade. The parade and festivities usually take place over the course of the weekend usually the first or second weekend in October in Jacksonville's Riverside neighborhood. The first pride parade was held in 1978.</p>
<p>A number of cultural events are also held in Jacksonville. The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Jazz_Festival" title="Jacksonville Jazz Festival">Jacksonville Jazz Festival</a>, held downtown, is the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> festival in the nation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/Springing_the_Blues" title="Springing the Blues">Springing the Blues</a></i>, one of the oldest and largest <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a> festivals, has been held in <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Beach,_Florida" title="Jacksonville Beach, Florida">Jacksonville Beach</a> since 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_of_Nations_Celebration" title="World of Nations Celebration">World of Nations Celebration</a> has been held in <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Park" title="Metropolitan Park">Metropolitan Park</a> since 1993, and features a number of events, food and souvenirs from various countries.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hemming_Plaza2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Hemming_Plaza2.JPG/220px-Hemming_Plaza2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Hemming_Plaza2.JPG/330px-Hemming_Plaza2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Hemming_Plaza2.JPG/440px-Hemming_Plaza2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hemming_Plaza2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hemming_Park" title="Hemming Park">Hemming Park</a> plays host to a variety of cultural events throughout the year.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Art Walk, a monthly outdoor art festival on the first Wednesday of each month, is sponsored by Downtown Vision, Inc, an organization which works to promote artistic talent and venues on the First Coast. Other events include the <a href="/wiki/Blessing_of_the_Fleet" title="Blessing of the Fleet">Blessing of the Fleet</a> held in March since 1985 and the Greater Jacksonville Agricultural Fair in November at the Jacksonville Fairgrounds and Exposition Center featuring games, rides, food, entertainment and livestock exhibition. <a href="/wiki/One_Spark" title="One Spark">One Spark</a> is an annual and the largest <a href="/wiki/Crowdfunding" title="Crowdfunding">crowdfunding</a> event held for creators to showcase their ideas for a chance to win part of $300,000 in funding. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverside_Arts_Market_(RAM)" title="Riverside Arts Market (RAM)">Riverside Arts Market (RAM)</a>, an outdoor arts-and-crafts market on the Riverwalk, occurs every Saturday from March to December under the canopy of the Fuller Warren Bridge. Holiday celebrations include the Freedom, Fanfare &amp; Fireworks celebration on <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(United_States)" title="Independence Day (United States)">July 4</a>, the lighting of Jacksonville's official <a href="/wiki/Christmas_tree" title="Christmas tree">Christmas tree</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Landing" title="Jacksonville Landing">Jacksonville Landing</a> on the day after <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving_(United_States)" title="Thanksgiving (United States)">Thanksgiving</a> and the Jacksonville Light Parade of boats the following day.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Veterans_Memorial_Arena" title="Jacksonville Veterans Memorial Arena">Jacksonville Veterans Memorial Arena</a>, which opened in 2003, is a 16,000-seat performance venue that attracts national entertainment, sporting events and also houses the Jacksonville Sports Hall of Fame. It replaced the outdated <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Coliseum" title="Jacksonville Coliseum">Jacksonville Coliseum</a> that was built in 1960 and demolished on June 26, 2003. The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Zoo_and_Gardens" title="Jacksonville Zoo and Gardens">Jacksonville Zoo and Gardens</a> boasts the second largest animal collection in the state. The zoo features <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">elephants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lions</a>, and, of course, <a href="/wiki/Jaguar" title="Jaguar">jaguars</a> (with an exhibit, <i>Range of the Jaguar</i>, hosted by the former owners of the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Jaguars" title="Jacksonville Jaguars">Jacksonville Jaguars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Weaver" title="Wayne Weaver">Delores and Wayne Weaver</a>). It also has a multitude of reptile houses, free flight aviaries, and many other animals. <a href="/wiki/Adventure_Landing" title="Adventure Landing">Adventure Landing</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Amusement_park" title="Amusement park">amusement park</a> with locations in Jacksonville and Jacksonville Beach. The Jacksonville Beach location contains Shipwreck Island, Duval County's only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterpark" title="Waterpark">waterpark</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Theatre_Jacksonville" title="Theatre Jacksonville">Theatre Jacksonville</a> was organized in 1919 as the <i>Little Theatre</i> and is one of the oldest continually producing <a href="/wiki/Community_theatre" title="Community theatre">community theatres</a> in the United States. The <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Dinner_Theatre" title="Alhambra Dinner Theatre">Alhambra Dinner Theatre</a>, located on the Southside near the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Florida" title="University of North Florida">University of North Florida</a>, has offered professional productions that frequently starred well-known actors since 1967. There are also a number of popular community theatres such as <i>Players by the Sea</i> located in Jacksonville Beach. The Murray Hill Art Center was reopened in February 2012 through a partnership of the Jacksonville Parks and Recreation (JaxParks) and the Art League of Jacksonville, a nonprofit dedicated to arts education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> The center is located in the historic Murray Hill area and offers community arts classes as well as shared studio space for aspiring artists. Visitors are welcomed year around for events and classes.</p>
<p>Jacksonville has two fully enclosed <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">shopping malls</a>. The oldest is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regency_Square_Mall_(Jacksonville,_Florida)" title="Regency Square Mall (Jacksonville, Florida)">Regency Square Mall</a>, which opened in 1967 and is located on former sand dunes in the Arlington area. The other is <a href="/wiki/The_Avenues_(shopping_mall)" title="The Avenues (shopping mall)">The Avenues Mall</a>, which opened in 1990 on the Southside, at the intersection of I-95 and US 1. The Orange Park Mall is another mall located just south of the city in the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Orange_Park,_Florida" title="Orange Park, Florida">Orange Park, Florida</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Clay_County,_Florida" title="Clay County, Florida">Clay County</a>, off of <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_21" title="Florida State Road 21">Blanding Boulevard</a> (State Road 21). The end of the indoor shopping mall may be indicated by the opening of The <a href="/wiki/St._Johns_Town_Center" title="St. Johns Town Center">St. Johns Town Center</a> in 2005 and the <a href="/wiki/River_City_Marketplace" title="River City Marketplace">River City Marketplace</a>, on the Northside in 2006. Both of these are "open air" malls, with a similar mix of stores, but without being contained under a single, enclosed roof. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Council_of_Shopping_Centers" title="International Council of Shopping Centers">International Council of Shopping Centers</a> (ICSC), only one enclosed mall has been built in the United States since 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-REMEMBER_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-REMEMBER-151">[149]</a></sup> The Avenues, Orange Park Mall, and St. Johns Town Center are all owned by <a href="/wiki/Simon_Property_Group" title="Simon Property Group">Simon Property Group</a>; Regency is owned by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Growth_Properties" title="General Growth Properties">General Growth Properties</a>; River City Marketplace is owned by <a href="/wiki/Ramco-Gershenson_Properties_Trust" title="Ramco-Gershenson Properties Trust">Ramco-Gershenson</a>.</p>
<h3><span id="Literature,_film_and_television"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature.2C_film_and_television">Literature, film and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Literature, film and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Media in Jacksonville, Florida">Media in Jacksonville, Florida</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GaumontStudios.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="452" data-file-width="600" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/GaumontStudios.jpg/220px-GaumontStudios.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/GaumontStudios.jpg/330px-GaumontStudios.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/GaumontStudios.jpg/440px-GaumontStudios.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GaumontStudios.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Motion picture scene at <a href="/wiki/Gaumont_Film_Company" title="Gaumont Film Company">Gaumont Studios</a>, 1910</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A handful of significant literary works are associated with Jacksonville and the surrounding area. Perhaps the most important of these is that of <a href="/wiki/James_Weldon_Johnson" title="James Weldon Johnson">James Weldon Johnson</a>. His first success as a writer was the poem "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lift_Ev%27ry_Voice_and_Sing" title="Lift Ev'ry Voice and Sing">Lift Ev'ry Voice and Sing</a>" (1899), which his brother Rosamond set to music; the song became unofficially known as the "Negro National Anthem."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup> Already famous for having written <i><a href="/wiki/Uncle_Tom%27s_Cabin" title="Uncle Tom's Cabin">Uncle Tom's Cabin</a></i> (1852), <a href="/wiki/Harriet_Beecher_Stowe" title="Harriet Beecher Stowe">Harriet Beecher Stowe</a> published <i><a href="/wiki/Palmetto_Leaves" title="Palmetto Leaves">Palmetto Leaves</a></i> in 1873. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Travel_guide" title="Travel guide">travel guide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Memoir" title="Memoir">memoir</a> about her winters in the town of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandarin,_Florida" title="Mandarin, Florida">Mandarin, Florida</a>, it was one of the first guides written about Florida and stimulated Florida's first boom of tourism and residential development in the 1880s.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sun-Ray_Cinema" title="Sun-Ray Cinema">Sun-Ray Cinema</a>, formerly the 5 Points Theatre and Riverside Theatre, opened in 1927. It was the first theater equipped to show talking pictures in Florida and the third nationally. It is located in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Five_Points_(Jacksonville)" title="Five Points (Jacksonville)">Five Points</a> section of town and was renamed the <i>Five Points Theater</i> in 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Florida_Theatre" title="Florida Theatre">Florida Theatre</a>, opened in 1927, is located in downtown Jacksonville and is one of only four remaining high-style movie palaces built in Florida during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Revival_Style_architecture" title="Mediterranean Revival Style architecture">Mediterranean Revival architectural</a> boom of the 1920s. Since that time, Jacksonville has been chosen by a number of film and television studios for on-location shooting. Notable motion pictures that have been partially or completely shot in Jacksonville since the silent film era include <i><a href="/wiki/Creature_from_the_Black_Lagoon" title="Creature from the Black Lagoon">Creature from the Black Lagoon</a></i> (1954), <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Adventures_of_Pippi_Longstocking" title="The New Adventures of Pippi Longstocking">The New Adventures of Pippi Longstocking</a></i> (1988), <i><a href="/wiki/Brenda_Starr_(film)" title="Brenda Starr (film)">Brenda Starr</a></i> (1989), <i><a href="/wiki/G.I._Jane" title="G.I. Jane">G.I. Jane</a></i> (1997), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Devil%27s_Advocate_(1997_film)" title="The Devil's Advocate (1997 film)">The Devil's Advocate</a></i> (1997), <i>Ride</i> (1998), <i><a href="/wiki/Why_Do_Fools_Fall_in_Love_(film)" title="Why Do Fools Fall in Love (film)">Why Do Fools Fall In Love</a></i> (1998), <i><a href="/wiki/Forces_of_Nature" title="Forces of Nature">Forces of Nature</a></i> (1999), <i><a href="/wiki/Tigerland" title="Tigerland">Tigerland</a></i> (2000), <i><a href="/wiki/Sunshine_State_(film)" title="Sunshine State (film)">Sunshine State</a></i> (2002), <i><a href="/wiki/Basic_(film)" title="Basic (film)">Basic</a></i> (2003), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Manchurian_Candidate_(2004_film)" title="The Manchurian Candidate (2004 film)">The Manchurian Candidate</a></i> (2004), <i><a href="/wiki/Lonely_Hearts_(2006_film)" title="Lonely Hearts (2006 film)">Lonely Hearts</a></i> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/Moving_McAllister" title="Moving McAllister">Moving McAllister</a></i> (2007), <i>The Year of Getting to Know Us</i> (2008), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ramen_Girl" title="The Ramen Girl">The Ramen Girl</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Like_Dandelion_Dust" title="Like Dandelion Dust">Like Dandelion Dust</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Movies_Filmed_in_Jacksonville_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Movies_Filmed_in_Jacksonville-155">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>Notable television series or made-for-television films that have been partially or completely shot in Jacksonville include <i><a href="/wiki/Inherit_the_Wind_(1988_film)" title="Inherit the Wind (1988 film)">Inherit the Wind</a></i> (1988), <i><a href="/wiki/Orpheus_Descending" title="Orpheus Descending">Orpheus Descending</a></i> (1990), <i><a href="/wiki/Saved_by_the_Light" title="Saved by the Light">Saved by the Light</a></i> (1995), <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Babysitter%27s_Seduction&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Babysitter's Seduction (page does not exist)">The Babysitter's Seduction</a></i> (1996),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/First_Time_Felon" title="First Time Felon">First Time Felon</a></i> (1997), <i><a href="/wiki/Safe_Harbor_(film)" title="Safe Harbor (film)">Safe Harbor</a></i> (2009), <i><a href="/wiki/Recount_(film)" title="Recount (film)">Recount</a></i> (2008), <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> (2009), and <i><a href="/wiki/Ash_vs_Evil_Dead" title="Ash vs Evil Dead">Ash vs Evil Dead</a></i> (2015).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_art_galleries">Museums and art galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Museums and art galleries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cummer_Museum,_Jacksonville,_FL,_US_(02).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Cummer_Museum%2C_Jacksonville%2C_FL%2C_US_%2802%29.jpg/220px-Cummer_Museum%2C_Jacksonville%2C_FL%2C_US_%2802%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Cummer_Museum%2C_Jacksonville%2C_FL%2C_US_%2802%29.jpg/330px-Cummer_Museum%2C_Jacksonville%2C_FL%2C_US_%2802%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Cummer_Museum%2C_Jacksonville%2C_FL%2C_US_%2802%29.jpg/440px-Cummer_Museum%2C_Jacksonville%2C_FL%2C_US_%2802%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cummer_Museum,_Jacksonville,_FL,_US_(02).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cummer_Museum_of_Art_and_Gardens" title="Cummer Museum of Art and Gardens">Cummer Museum of Art and Gardens</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cummer_Museum_of_Art_and_Gardens" title="Cummer Museum of Art and Gardens">Cummer Museum of Art and Gardens</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Art_museum" title="Art museum">art museum</a> in Jacksonville's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverside,_Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Riverside, Jacksonville, Florida">Riverside</a> neighborhood. It was founded in 1961, following the death of Ninah Mae Holden Cummer, who willed her collection, home, and gardens to the museum. Its galleries display one of the world's three most comprehensive collections of <a href="/wiki/Meissen_porcelain" title="Meissen porcelain">Meissen porcelain</a> as well as large collections of American, European, and Japanese art. The grounds also contain two acres of Italian and English gardens begun by Ninah Cummer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-museums_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-museums-157">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Contemporary_Art_Jacksonville" title="Museum of Contemporary Art Jacksonville">Museum of Contemporary Art Jacksonville</a> (MOCA Jacksonville) is a <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary art</a> museum funded and operated as a "cultural resource" of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Florida" title="University of North Florida">University of North Florida</a>. Tracing its roots back to the formation of Jacksonville's Fine Arts Society in 1924, it opened its current 60,000-square-foot (6,000 m<sup>2</sup>) facility next to the Main Library downtown in 2003. The museum features eclectic permanent and traveling exhibitions and a collection of over 700 works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-museums_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-museums-157">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museum_of_Science_%26_History" title="Museum of Science &amp; History">Museum of Science &amp; History</a> (MOSH), located in downtown's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southbank_Riverwalk" title="Southbank Riverwalk">Southbank Riverwalk</a>, specializes in science and local history exhibits. It features a main exhibit that changes quarterly, plus three floors of nature exhibits, an extensive exhibit on the history of Northeast Florida, a hands-on science area and the area's only <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a> theater, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bryan_Gooding_Planetarium" title="Bryan Gooding Planetarium">Bryan Gooding Planetarium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-museums_157-2"><a href="#cite_note-museums-157">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Planetarium_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Planetarium-159">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kingsley_Plantation" title="Kingsley Plantation">Kingsley Plantation</a> is a historic <a href="/wiki/Plantations_in_the_American_South" title="Plantations in the American South">plantation</a> built in 1798. The house of <a href="/wiki/Zephaniah_Kingsley" title="Zephaniah Kingsley">Zephaniah Kingsley</a>, barn, kitchen and slave cabins still exist today.</p>
<p>Alexander Brest, founder of Duval Engineering and Contracting Co., was also the benefactor for the <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Brest_Museum_and_Gallery" title="Alexander Brest Museum and Gallery">Alexander Brest Museum and Gallery</a> on the campus of <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_University" title="Jacksonville University">Jacksonville University</a>. The exhibits are a diverse collection of <a href="/wiki/Ivory_carving" title="Ivory carving">carved ivory</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian" title="Pre-Columbian">Pre-Columbian</a> artifacts, <a href="/wiki/Steuben_Glass_Works" title="Steuben Glass Works">Steuben glass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_ceramics" title="Chinese ceramics">Chinese porcelain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cloisonn%C3%A9" title="Cloisonné">Cloisonné</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiffany_glass" title="Tiffany glass">Tiffany glass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Marshall_Boehm" title="Edward Marshall Boehm">Boehm</a> porcelain and rotating exhibitions containing the work of local, regional, national and international artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Maritime_Museum" title="Jacksonville Maritime Museum">Jacksonville Maritime Museum</a>, located in the Jacksonville Landing, includes models of ships, paintings, photographs and artifacts dating to 1562.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>Three other art galleries are located at educational institutions in town. <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_College_at_Jacksonville" title="Florida State College at Jacksonville">Florida State College at Jacksonville</a> has the Kent Gallery on their westside campus and the Wilson Center for the Arts at their main campus. The University Gallery is located on the campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Florida" title="University of North Florida">University of North Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Jacksonville <a href="/wiki/Karpeles_Manuscript_Library_Museum_(Jacksonville)" title="Karpeles Manuscript Library Museum (Jacksonville)">Karpeles Manuscript Library Museum</a> is a branch of the world's largest private collection of original manuscripts and documents. The museum in Jacksonville is in a 1921 neoclassical building on the outskirts of downtown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> In addition to document displays, there is also an antique-book library, with volumes dating from the late 19th century.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catherine_Street_Fire_Station" title="Catherine Street Fire Station">Catherine Street Fire Station</a> building is on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a> and was relocated to Metropolitan Park in 1993. It houses the Jacksonville Fire Museum and features 500+ artifacts including an 1806 hand pumper.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/LaVilla_Museum" title="LaVilla Museum">LaVilla Museum</a> opened in 1999 and features a permanent display of African-American history. The art exhibits are changed periodically.</p>
<p>There are also several historical properties and items of interest in the city, including the Klutho Building, the <a href="/wiki/Morocco_Temple" title="Morocco Temple">Old Morocco Temple Building</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Palm_and_Cycad_Arboretum" title="Palm and Cycad Arboretum">Palm and Cycad Arboretum</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_F._Osborn_III_Convention_Center" title="Prime F. Osborn III Convention Center">Prime F. Osborn III Convention Center</a>, originally built as Union Station train depot. The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Historical_Society" title="Jacksonville Historical Society">Jacksonville Historical Society</a> showcases two restoration projects: the 1887 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Andrew%27s_Episcopal_Church_(Jacksonville,_Florida)" title="St. Andrew's Episcopal Church (Jacksonville, Florida)">St. Andrews Episcopal Church</a> and the 1879 Merrill House, both located near the sports complex.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Florida_Theater.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Florida_Theater.JPG/220px-Florida_Theater.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Florida_Theater.JPG/330px-Florida_Theater.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Florida_Theater.JPG/440px-Florida_Theater.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Florida_Theater.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_XX" title="The XX">The XX</a> performing at the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Theatre" title="Florida Theatre">Florida Theatre</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ritz_Theatre_(Jacksonville)" title="Ritz Theatre (Jacksonville)">Ritz Theatre</a>, opened in 1929, is located in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LaVilla,_Jacksonville,_Florida" title="LaVilla, Jacksonville, Florida">LaVilla</a> neighborhood of the northern part of Jacksonville's downtown. The Jacksonville music scene was active in the 1930s in LaVilla, which was known as "Harlem of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">South</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup> Black musicians from across the country visited Jacksonville to play standing room only performances at the <a href="/wiki/Ritz_Theatre_(Jacksonville)" title="Ritz Theatre (Jacksonville)">Ritz Theatre</a> and the <i>Knights of Pythias Hall</i>. <a href="/wiki/Cab_Calloway" title="Cab Calloway">Cab Calloway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_Ellington" title="Duke Ellington">Duke Ellington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ella_Fitzgerald" title="Ella Fitzgerald">Ella Fitzgerald</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armstrong" title="Louis Armstrong">Louis Armstrong</a> were a few of the legendary performers who appeared. After his mother died when he was 15, <a href="/wiki/Ray_Charles" title="Ray Charles">Ray Charles</a> lived with friends of his mother while he played piano at the Ritz for a year, before moving on to fame and fortune. The Ritz Theatre was rebuilt and opened in October 1999.</p>
<p>Jacksonville native <a href="/wiki/Pat_Boone" title="Pat Boone">Pat Boone</a> was a popular 1950s singer and teen idol. During the 1960s, the <a href="/wiki/Classics_IV" title="Classics IV">Classics IV</a> was the most successful pop rock band from Jacksonville. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Rock" title="Southern Rock">Southern Rock</a> was defined by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allman_Brothers_Band" title="Allman Brothers Band">Allman Brothers Band</a>, which formed in 1969 in Jacksonville. <a href="/wiki/Lynyrd_Skynyrd" title="Lynyrd Skynyrd">Lynyrd Skynyrd</a> achieved near cult status and inspired <a href="/wiki/Blackfoot_(band)" title="Blackfoot (band)">Blackfoot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molly_Hatchet" title="Molly Hatchet">Molly Hatchet</a> and <a href="/wiki/38_Special_(band)" title="38 Special (band)">.38 Special</a>, all successful in the 1970s. The 1980s were a quiet decade for musical talent in Jacksonville.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Times-Union_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Times-Union Center for the Performing Arts">Times-Union Center for the Performing Arts</a> consists of three distinct halls: the <i>Jim &amp; Jan Moran Theater</i>, a venue for touring Broadway shows; the <i>Jacoby Symphony Hall</i>, home of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Jacksonville Symphony Orchestra">Jacksonville Symphony Orchestra</a>; and the <i>Terry Theater</i>, intended for small shows and recitals. The building was originally erected as the Civic Auditorium in 1962 and underwent a major renovation and construction in 1996.</p>
<p>The next local group to achieve national success was the <a href="/wiki/Nu_metal" title="Nu metal">nu metal</a> band <a href="/wiki/Limp_Bizkit" title="Limp Bizkit">Limp Bizkit</a>, formed in 1994. Other popular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hip_Hop" title="Hip Hop">Hip Hop</a> acts in the 1990s included <a href="/wiki/95_South" title="95 South">95 South</a>, <a href="/wiki/69_Boyz" title="69 Boyz">69 Boyz</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Quad_City_DJ%27s" title="Quad City DJ's">Quad City DJ's</a>. The bands <a href="/wiki/Inspection_12" title="Inspection 12">Inspection 12</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cold_(band)" title="Cold (band)">Cold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yellowcard" title="Yellowcard">Yellowcard</a> were also well known and had a large following. Following the millennium, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fit_For_Rivals" title="Fit For Rivals">Fit For Rivals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burn_Season" title="Burn Season">Burn Season</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evergreen_Terrace" title="Evergreen Terrace">Evergreen Terrace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shinedown" title="Shinedown">Shinedown</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Red_Jumpsuit_Apparatus" title="The Red Jumpsuit Apparatus">The Red Jumpsuit Apparatus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Black_Kids" title="Black Kids">Black Kids</a> became notable bands from the city.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Jacksonville" title="Sports in Jacksonville">Sports in Jacksonville</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JaguarsEverbank15.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="655" data-file-width="873" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/JaguarsEverbank15.jpg/220px-JaguarsEverbank15.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/JaguarsEverbank15.jpg/330px-JaguarsEverbank15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/JaguarsEverbank15.jpg/440px-JaguarsEverbank15.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JaguarsEverbank15.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/The_Star-Spangled_Banner" title="The Star-Spangled Banner">The Star-Spangled Banner</a> performed before a <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Jaguars" title="Jacksonville Jaguars">Jacksonville Jaguars</a> game at <a href="/wiki/EverBank_Field" title="EverBank Field">EverBank Field</a>.</div>
</div>
