<p>Jacksonville is home to one <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">major league</a> <a href="/wiki/Professional_sports" title="Professional sports">sports team</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Jaguars" title="Jacksonville Jaguars">Jacksonville Jaguars</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL). The Jaguars joined the NFL as an <a href="/wiki/Expansion_team" title="Expansion team">expansion team</a> in the 1995 season; they play their home games at <a href="/wiki/EverBank_Field" title="EverBank Field">EverBank Field</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup> In 2005, Jacksonville hosted <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXIX" title="Super Bowl XXXIX">Super Bowl XXXIX</a>. The <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour" title="PGA Tour">PGA Tour</a>, which organizes the main professional <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> tournaments in the U.S., is headquartered in the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Ponte_Vedra_Beach,_Florida" title="Ponte Vedra Beach, Florida">Ponte Vedra Beach</a>, where it holds <a href="/wiki/The_Players_Championship" title="The Players Championship">The Players Championship</a> every year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jacksonville is also home to several <a href="/wiki/Minor_league" title="Minor league">minor league</a>-level teams. The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Jumbo_Shrimp" title="Jacksonville Jumbo Shrimp">Jacksonville Jumbo Shrimp</a>, a class <a href="/wiki/Double-A_(baseball)" title="Double-A (baseball)">Double-A</a> <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> team, have played in Jacksonville continuously since 1970, longer than any other Double-A team has been in its city, and are the top-selling franchise in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_League_(baseball)" title="Southern League (baseball)">Southern League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pahigian201_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pahigian201-168">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jumbo_Shrimp_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jumbo_Shrimp-169">[167]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Sharks" title="Jacksonville Sharks">Jacksonville Sharks</a>, who began play in 2010, were the champions of the <a href="/wiki/Arena_Football_League" title="Arena Football League">Arena Football League</a>'s <a href="/wiki/ArenaBowl_XXIV" title="ArenaBowl XXIV">ArenaBowl XXIV</a> in 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> and now play in the <a href="/wiki/National_Arena_League" title="National Arena League">National Arena League</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Axemen" title="Jacksonville Axemen">Jacksonville Axemen</a> are a semi-professional <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> team founded in 2006, and now play in the <a href="/wiki/USA_Rugby_League" title="USA Rugby League">USA Rugby League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Code13_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-Code13-172">[170]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Giants" title="Jacksonville Giants">Jacksonville Giants</a> <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> team started play in the new <a href="/wiki/American_Basketball_Association_(2000%E2%80%93present)" title="American Basketball Association (2000–present)">American Basketball Association</a> in December 2010. The Giants won the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_ABA_season" title="2011–12 ABA season">2012 ABA Championship</a> in March 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa, Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Armada_FC" title="Jacksonville Armada FC">Jacksonville Armada FC</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer">soccer</a> team that began play in the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Soccer_League" title="North American Soccer League">North American Soccer League</a> (NASL) in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_sports" title="College sports">College sports</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a>, are popular in Jacksonville. The city hosts the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida%E2%80%93Georgia_game" title="Florida–Georgia game">Florida–Georgia game</a>, an annual <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> game between the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida">University of Florida</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Georgia" title="University of Georgia">University of Georgia</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gator_Bowl" title="Gator Bowl">Gator Bowl</a>, a post-season college <a href="/wiki/Bowl_game" title="Bowl game">bowl game</a>. Jacksonville's two universities compete in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a>: the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Florida" title="University of North Florida">University of North Florida</a> <a href="/wiki/North_Florida_Ospreys" title="North Florida Ospreys">Ospreys</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_University" title="Jacksonville University">Jacksonville University</a> <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Dolphins" title="Jacksonville Dolphins">Dolphins</a>, both in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Sun_Conference" title="Atlantic Sun Conference">Atlantic Sun Conference</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Jacksonville" title="Government of Jacksonville">Government of Jacksonville</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jacksonville_City_Hall_(South_face).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3864" data-file-width="5152" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Jacksonville_City_Hall_%28South_face%29.JPG/220px-Jacksonville_City_Hall_%28South_face%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Jacksonville_City_Hall_%28South_face%29.JPG/330px-Jacksonville_City_Hall_%28South_face%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Jacksonville_City_Hall_%28South_face%29.JPG/440px-Jacksonville_City_Hall_%28South_face%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jacksonville_City_Hall_(South_face).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/St._James_Building" title="St. James Building">St. James Building</a>, currently housing Jacksonville City Hall.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The most noteworthy feature of Jacksonville government is its consolidated nature, an arrangement brought about in the 1968 <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Consolidation" title="Jacksonville Consolidation">Jacksonville Consolidation</a>. The Duval County-Jacksonville consolidation eliminated any type of separate county <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a> or <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a>, and supplanted these positions with the Mayor of Jacksonville and the City Council of the City of Jacksonville, respectively. Because of this, voters who live <i>outside</i> of the city limits of Jacksonville but <i>inside</i> Duval County are allowed to vote in elections for these positions and to run for them. In fact, in 1995, <a href="/wiki/John_Delaney_(Florida_politician)" title="John Delaney (Florida politician)">John Delaney</a>, a resident of <a href="/wiki/Neptune_Beach,_Florida" title="Neptune Beach, Florida">Neptune Beach</a>, was elected mayor of the city of Jacksonville.</p>
<p>Jacksonville is organized under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_charter" title="City charter">city charter</a> and provides for a "strong" <a href="/wiki/Mayor%E2%80%93council_government" title="Mayor–council government">mayor–council</a> form of city government. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Jacksonville" title="Mayor of Jacksonville">Mayor of Jacksonville</a> is elected to four-year terms and serves as the head of the government's executive branch. The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_City_Council" title="Jacksonville City Council">Jacksonville City Council</a> comprises nineteen members, fourteen representing <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district" title="Electoral district">electoral districts</a> and five more in <a href="/wiki/At-large" title="At-large">at-large</a> seats. The mayor oversees most city departments, though some are independent or quasi-independent. Law enforcement is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Sheriff%27s_Office" title="Jacksonville Sheriff's Office">Jacksonville Sheriff's Office</a>, headed by an elected <a href="/wiki/Sheriff" title="Sheriff">sheriff</a>, public schools are overseen by <a href="/wiki/Duval_County_Public_Schools" title="Duval County Public Schools">Duval County Public Schools</a>, and several services are provided by largely independent authorities. The mayor holds veto power over all resolutions and ordinances made by the city council and also has the power to hire and fire the head of various city departments.</p>
<p>Some government services remained—as they had been before consolidation—independent of both city and county authority. In accordance with Florida law, the school board continues to exist with nearly complete autonomy. Jacksonville also has several quasi-independent government agencies which only nominally answer to the consolidated authority, including <a href="/wiki/JEA" title="JEA">electric authority</a>, port authority, transportation authority, housing authority and airport authority. The main environmental and agricultural body is the Duval County Soil and Water Conservation District, which works closely with other area and state agencies.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Housing_Authority" title="Jacksonville Housing Authority">Jacksonville Housing Authority</a> (JHA) is the quasi-independent agency responsible for <a href="/wiki/Public_housing" title="Public housing">public housing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Subsidized_housing" title="Subsidized housing">subsidized housing</a> in Jacksonville. The Mayor and City Council of Jacksonville established the JHA in 1994 to create an effective, community service oriented, public housing agency with innovative ideas and a different attitude. The primary goal was to provide safe, clean, affordable housing for eligible low and moderate income families, the elderly, and persons with disabilities. The secondary goal was to provide effective social services, work with residents to improve their quality of life, encourage employment and self-sufficiency, and help residents move out of assisted housing. To that end, JHA works with <a href="/wiki/HabiJax" title="HabiJax">HabiJax</a> to help low and moderate income families to escape the public housing cycle and become successful, productive, homeowners and taxpayers.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Politics_of_Jacksonville" title="Politics of Jacksonville">Politics of Jacksonville</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LennyCurryJAX.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="489" data-file-width="350" height="307" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/LennyCurryJAX.jpg/220px-LennyCurryJAX.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/LennyCurryJAX.jpg/330px-LennyCurryJAX.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/33/LennyCurryJAX.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LennyCurryJAX.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lenny_Curry" title="Lenny Curry">Lenny Curry</a>, the current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Jacksonville" title="Mayor of Jacksonville">Mayor of Jacksonville</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The present mayor is <a href="/wiki/Lenny_Curry" title="Lenny Curry">Lenny Curry</a>, who assumed office on July 1, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup> The past mayor was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alvin_Brown_(politician)" title="Alvin Brown (politician)">Alvin Brown</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gibbonshistory_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gibbonshistory-180">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>Federally, most of the city is in the <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_4th_congressional_district" title="Florida's 4th congressional district">4th district</a>, represented by Republican <a href="/wiki/John_Rutherford_(Florida_politician)" title="John Rutherford (Florida politician)">John Rutherford</a>. Most of central Jacksonville is in the <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_5th_congressional_district" title="Florida's 5th congressional district">5th district</a>, represented by Democrat <a href="/wiki/Al_Lawson" title="Al Lawson">Al Lawson</a>. The 4th and 5th districts are some of the most <a href="/wiki/Gerrymandering" title="Gerrymandering">gerrymandered</a> districts in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, Duval County's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crime_rate" title="Crime rate">crime rate</a> was 5,106 per 100,000 people, according to the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Department_of_Law_Enforcement" title="Florida Department of Law Enforcement">Florida Department of Law Enforcement</a>. The county's <a href="/wiki/Murder" title="Murder">murder</a> rate had been the highest among Florida's counties with a population of 500,000 or more for eleven years in 2009, leading to widespread discussion in the community about how to deal with the problem. In 2010 Duval County's violent crime rate decreased by 9.3% from the previous year, with total crime decreasing 7.3%, putting the murder rate behind that of <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">Miami-Dade County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jacksonville and Duval County historically maintained separate police agencies: the Jacksonville Police Department and Duval County Sheriff's Office. As part of consolidation in 1968, the two merged, creating the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Sheriff%27s_Office" title="Jacksonville Sheriff's Office">Jacksonville Sheriff's Office</a> (JSO). The JSO is headed by the elected Sheriff of Jacksonville, currently <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Williams_(sheriff)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mike Williams (sheriff) (page does not exist)">Mike Williams</a>, and is responsible for law enforcement and corrections in the county.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Education in Jacksonville, Florida">Education in Jacksonville, Florida</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_metropolitan_Jacksonville" title="List of colleges and universities in metropolitan Jacksonville">List of colleges and universities in metropolitan Jacksonville</a>.</div>
<p>Jacksonville is home to a number of institutions of higher education. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Florida" title="University of North Florida">University of North Florida</a> (UNF), opened in 1972, is a public institution and a member of the <a href="/wiki/State_University_System_of_Florida" title="State University System of Florida">State University System of Florida</a>. Former mayor <a href="/wiki/John_Delaney_(Florida_politician)" title="John Delaney (Florida politician)">John Delaney</a> has been president of UNF since 2003. <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_University" title="Jacksonville University">Jacksonville University</a> (JU) is a private institution founded in 1934. <a href="/wiki/Edward_Waters_College" title="Edward Waters College">Edward Waters College</a>, established in 1866, is the oldest college in Jacksonville and the state's oldest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historically_black_college" title="Historically black college">historically black college</a>. <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_College_at_Jacksonville" title="Florida State College at Jacksonville">Florida State College at Jacksonville</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_university" title="State university">state college</a> and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_College_System" title="Florida College System">Florida College System</a>, offering two-year <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associate%27s_degree" title="Associate's degree">associate's degrees</a> as well as some four-year <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degrees" title="Bachelor's degrees">bachelor's degrees</a>. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida">University of Florida</a> has its second campus of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J._Hillis_Miller_Health_Science_Center" title="J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center">J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center</a> in Jacksonville.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other colleges and universities in Jacksonville include <a href="/wiki/Florida_Coastal_School_of_Law" title="Florida Coastal School of Law">Florida Coastal School of Law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jones_College_(Jacksonville)" title="Jones College (Jacksonville)">Jones College</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup> Also in the area are <a href="/wiki/St._Johns_River_State_College" title="St. Johns River State College">St. Johns River State College</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_university" title="State university">state college</a> with campuses in <a href="/wiki/Clay_County,_Florida" title="Clay County, Florida">Clay</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Johns_County,_Florida" title="St. Johns County, Florida">St. Johns</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Putnam_County,_Florida" title="Putnam County, Florida">Putnam</a> Counties, and <a href="/wiki/Flagler_College" title="Flagler College">Flagler College</a> in <a href="/wiki/St._Augustine,_Florida" title="St. Augustine, Florida">St. Augustine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup></p>

<div style="width: 155px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_education">Primary and secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Duval_County_Public_Schools" title="Duval County Public Schools">Duval County Public Schools</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_high_schools_in_Florida#Duval_County" title="List of high schools in Florida">List of high schools in Jacksonville</a></div>
<p>Public <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">primary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary</a> schools in Jacksonville and Duval County are administered by <a href="/wiki/Duval_County_Public_Schools" title="Duval County Public Schools">Duval County Public Schools</a>, which is governed by an elected, seven-member <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duval_County_School_Board" title="Duval County School Board">Duval County School Board</a>. In the 2009–2010 school year the district enrolled 123,000 students. It administers 172 total schools, including 103 <a href="/wiki/Elementary_school" title="Elementary school">elementary schools</a>, 25 <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">middle schools</a>, 19 <a href="/wiki/High_school_(North_America)" title="High school (North America)">high schools</a>, 3 K–8 schools, and 1 6–12 school, as well as 13 <a href="/wiki/Charter_school" title="Charter school">charter schools</a> and a juvenile justice school program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ourschools_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-ourschools-186">[184]</a></sup> Of these, 62 are designated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnet_schools" title="Magnet schools">magnet schools</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ourschools_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-ourschools-186">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>Three of Jacksonville's high schools, <a href="/wiki/Stanton_College_Preparatory_School" title="Stanton College Preparatory School">Stanton College Preparatory School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darnell-Cookman_School_of_the_Medical_Arts" title="Darnell-Cookman School of the Medical Arts">Darnell-Cookman School of the Medical Arts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paxon_School_for_Advanced_Studies" title="Paxon School for Advanced Studies">Paxon School for Advanced Studies</a> regularly appear at the top of <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> magazine's annual list of the country's top public high schools, coming in respectively at #3 #7, and #8 in the 2010 edition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEWSWEEK_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-NEWSWEEK-187">[185]</a></sup> Five other schools, <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Anderson_School_of_the_Arts" title="Douglas Anderson School of the Arts">Douglas Anderson School of the Arts</a> (#33), <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_High_School" title="Mandarin High School">Mandarin High School</a> (#97), <a href="/wiki/Duncan_U._Fletcher_High_School" title="Duncan U. Fletcher High School">Duncan U. Fletcher High School</a> (#205) <a href="/wiki/Sandalwood_High_School" title="Sandalwood High School">Sandalwood High School</a> (#210), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Englewood_High_School_(Jacksonville,_Florida)" title="Englewood High School (Jacksonville, Florida)">Englewood High School</a> (#1146) were also included in the list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEWSWEEK_187-1"><a href="#cite_note-NEWSWEEK-187">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_St._Augustine" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of St. Augustine">Roman Catholic Diocese of St. Augustine</a> operates a number of <a href="/wiki/Catholic_school" title="Catholic school">Catholic schools</a> in Jacksonville, including two high schools, <a href="/wiki/Bishop_Kenny_High_School" title="Bishop Kenny High School">Bishop Kenny High School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bishop_John_J._Snyder_High_School" title="Bishop John J. Snyder High School">Bishop John J. Snyder High School</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> Other private schools in Jacksonville include <a href="/wiki/Arlington_Country_Day_School" title="Arlington Country Day School">Arlington Country Day School</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bolles_School" title="Bolles School">Bolles School</a>, Trinity Christian Academy, and the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_School_of_Jacksonville" title="Episcopal School of Jacksonville">Episcopal School of Jacksonville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_libraries">Public libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Public libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Public_Library_(Florida)" title="Jacksonville Public Library (Florida)">Jacksonville Public Library (Florida)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jacksonville_library.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7d/Jacksonville_library.JPG/220px-Jacksonville_library.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7d/Jacksonville_library.JPG/330px-Jacksonville_library.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7d/Jacksonville_library.JPG/440px-Jacksonville_library.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jacksonville_library.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jacksonville Main Library.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Public_Library_(Florida)" title="Jacksonville Public Library (Florida)">Jacksonville Public Library</a> had its beginnings when May Moore and Florence Murphy started the "Jacksonville Library and Literary Association" in 1878. The Association was populated by various prominent Jacksonville residents and sought to create a free public library and reading room for the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jplhistory_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-jplhistory-190">[188]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over the course of 127 years, the system has grown from that one room library to become one of the largest in the state. The Jacksonville library system has twenty branches, ranging in size from the 54,000 sq ft (5,000 m<sup>2</sup>) West Regional Library to smaller neighborhood libraries like Westbrook and Eastside. The Library annually receives nearly 4 million visitors and circulates over 6 million items. Nearly 500,000 library cards are held by area residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jplprofile_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-jplprofile-191">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 12, 2005, the new 300,000 sq ft (30,000 m<sup>2</sup>) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Public_Library_(Florida)#Main_Library" title="Jacksonville Public Library (Florida)">Main Library</a> opened to the public, replacing the 40-year-old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haydon_Burns_Library" title="Haydon Burns Library">Haydon Burns Library</a>. The largest public library in the state, the opening of the new main library marked the completion of an unprecedented period of growth for the system under the <a href="/wiki/Better_Jacksonville_Plan" title="Better Jacksonville Plan">Better Jacksonville Plan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-betterjax_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-betterjax-192">[190]</a></sup> The new Main Library offers specialized reading rooms, public access to hundreds of computers and public displays of art, an extensive collection of books, and special collections ranging from the African-American Collection to the recently opened Holocaust Collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jplhistory_190-1"><a href="#cite_note-jplhistory-190">[188]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Transportation in Jacksonville, Florida">Transportation in Jacksonville, Florida</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DamesPBJFL.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="2592" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/DamesPBJFL.jpg/220px-DamesPBJFL.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/DamesPBJFL.jpg/330px-DamesPBJFL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/DamesPBJFL.jpg/440px-DamesPBJFL.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DamesPBJFL.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Dames_Point_Bridge" title="Dames Point Bridge">Dames Point Bridge</a> (officially the <b><a href="/wiki/Napoleon_B._Broward" title="Napoleon B. Broward">Napoleon Bonaparte Broward</a> Bridge</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Cable-stayed_bridge" title="Cable-stayed bridge">cable-stayed</a> <a href="/wiki/Bridge" title="Bridge">bridge</a> over the <a href="/wiki/St._Johns_River" title="St. Johns River">St. Johns River</a>. Construction began in 1985 and was completed in 1989.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roadways_and_bridges">Roadways and bridges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Roadways and bridges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There are seven bridges over the <a href="/wiki/St._Johns_River" title="St. Johns River">St. Johns River</a> at Jacksonville. They include (starting from furthest downstream) the <a href="/wiki/Dames_Point_Bridge" title="Dames Point Bridge">Napoleon Bonaparte Broward Bridge (Dames Point)</a> (which carries Interstate 295 Eastern Beltway traffic), the <a href="/wiki/Mathews_Bridge" title="Mathews Bridge">John E. Mathews Bridge</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hart_Bridge" title="Hart Bridge">Isaiah D. Hart Bridge</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Main_Street_Bridge_(Jacksonville)" title="Main Street Bridge (Jacksonville)">John T. Alsop Jr. Bridge (Main Street)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Acosta_Bridge" title="Acosta Bridge">St. Elmo W. Acosta Bridge</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fuller_Warren_Bridge" title="Fuller Warren Bridge">Fuller Warren Bridge</a> (which carries <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Florida" title="Interstate 95 in Florida">I-95</a> traffic) and the <a href="/wiki/Buckman_Bridge" title="Buckman Bridge">Henry Holland Buckman Bridge</a> (which carries <a href="/wiki/Interstate_295_(Florida)" title="Interstate 295 (Florida)">I-295 North/South</a> traffic). Also, next to the Acosta Bridge is a large jackknife railroad bridge built in the 1920s by Henry flagler's FEC railroad.</p>
<p>Beginning in 1953, tolls were charged on the Hart, Mathews, Fuller Warren and the Main Street bridges to pay for bridge construction, renovations and many other highway projects. As Jacksonville grew, toll plazas created bottlenecks and caused delays and accidents during rush hours. In 1988, Jacksonville voters chose to eliminate toll collection and replace the revenue with a ½ cent local sales tax increase. In 1989, the toll booths were removed.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Interstate_10_in_Florida" title="Interstate 10 in Florida">Interstate 10</a> (I-10) and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Florida" title="Interstate 95 in Florida">I-95</a> intersect in Jacksonville, forming the busiest intersection in the region with 200,000 vehicles each day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> I-10 ends at this intersection (the other end being in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Monica,_California" title="Santa Monica, California">Santa Monica, California</a>). Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_202" title="Florida State Road 202">State Road 202</a> (SR 202, J. Turner Butler Boulevard) connects Jacksonville to the beaches.</p>
<p>I-95 has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bypass_route" title="Bypass route">bypass route</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_295_(Florida)" title="Interstate 295 (Florida)">I-295</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Ring_road" title="Ring road">encircles</a> the downtown area. The major interchange at I-295 and SR 202 was finally completed on December 24, 2008. <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_9B" title="Florida State Road 9B">SR 9B</a> is under construction and will connect I-295's southeast corner to the Bayard Area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup> SR 9B will be called I-795 when it is completed. <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 1 in Florida">U.S. Highway 1</a> (US 1) and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_17_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 17 in Florida">US 17</a> travel through the city from the south to the north, and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_23_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 23 in Florida">US 23</a> enters the city <a href="/wiki/Concurrency_(road)" title="Concurrency (road)">running concurrently</a> with US 1. In downtown, US 23 splits from US 1 and quickly runs to its southern terminus. The eastern terminus of <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_90_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 90 in Florida">US 90</a> is in nearby <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Beach,_Florida" title="Jacksonville Beach, Florida">Jacksonville Beach</a> near the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>. US 23's other end is in <a href="/wiki/Mackinaw_City,_Michigan" title="Mackinaw City, Michigan">Mackinaw City, Michigan</a>.</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-3" style="-moz-column-count: 3; -webkit-column-count: 3; column-count: 3;">
<ul>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="601" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/I-10.svg/20px-I-10.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/I-10.svg/30px-I-10.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/I-10.svg/40px-I-10.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Interstate_10_in_Florida" title="Interstate 10 in Florida">I-10</a></span></li>

<li><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/US_1.svg/20px-US_1.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/US_1.svg/30px-US_1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/US_1.svg/40px-US_1.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 1 in Florida">US 1</a></span></li>

<li><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/US_90.svg/20px-US_90.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/US_90.svg/30px-US_90.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/US_90.svg/40px-US_90.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_90_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 90 in Florida">US 90</a></span></li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="750" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/US_301.svg/25px-US_301.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/US_301.svg/38px-US_301.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/US_301.svg/50px-US_301.svg.png 2x" width="25"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_301_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 301 in Florida">US 301</a></span></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p>Several regional transportation projects have been undertaken in recent years to deal with congestion on Jacksonville freeways. A $152 million project to create a high-speed interchange at the intersection of Interstates 10 and 95 began in February 2005, after the conclusion of <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXIX" title="Super Bowl XXXIX">Super Bowl XXXIX</a>. Construction was expected to take nearly six years with multiple lane flyovers and the requirement that the interchange remain open throughout the project. The previous configuration utilized single lane, low speed, curved ramps which created backups during rush hours and contributed to accidents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> Also, construction of 9B, future <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_795_(Florida)" title="Interstate 795 (Florida)">Interstate 795</a>, is currently underway.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transit_system">Transit system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Transit system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Transportation_Authority" title="Jacksonville Transportation Authority">Jacksonville Transportation Authority</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hemming_Plaza_Station1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Hemming_Plaza_Station1.JPG/170px-Hemming_Plaza_Station1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Hemming_Plaza_Station1.JPG/255px-Hemming_Plaza_Station1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Hemming_Plaza_Station1.JPG/340px-Hemming_Plaza_Station1.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hemming_Plaza_Station1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Skyway" title="Jacksonville Skyway">Jacksonville Skyway</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Skyway" title="Jacksonville Skyway">Jacksonville Skyway</a> is an automated <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">people mover</a> connecting <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_College_at_Jacksonville" title="Florida State College at Jacksonville">Florida State College at Jacksonville</a> downtown campus, the Northbank central business district, <a href="/wiki/Prime_F._Osborn_III_Convention_Center" title="Prime F. Osborn III Convention Center">Convention Center</a>, and Southbank locations. The system includes 8 stops connected by two lines. The existing train is a UMIII <a href="/wiki/Monorail" title="Monorail">monorail</a> built by Bombardier. The guideway consists of concrete beams which rest atop an unusually large support structure not used in most monorail systems. Maximum speed for the train is 48 km/h (30 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>A monorail was first proposed in the 1970s as part of a mobility plan hoping to attract interest from the Urban Mass Transit Administration's Downtown Peoplemover Program. The initial study was undertaken by the Florida Department of Transportation and Jacksonville's planning department, who took the Skyway project to the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Transportation_Authority" title="Jacksonville Transportation Authority">Jacksonville Transportation Authority</a> (JTA) in 1977. Following further development and a final 18-month feasibility study, the UMTA selected Jacksonville as one of seven cities to receive federal funding for an automated people mover. Two other related projects are Miami's Metromover and Detroit's People Mover. UMTA's approved plan called for the construction of a 2.5-mile (4.0 km) Phase I system to be built in three segments.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>, the national passenger rail system, provides daily service from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacksonville_(Amtrak_station)" title="Jacksonville (Amtrak station)">Jacksonville Amtrak Station</a> on Clifford Lane in the northwest section of the city. Two trains presently stop there, the <i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Meteor" title="Silver Meteor">Silver Meteor</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silver_Star_(passenger_train)" title="Silver Star (passenger train)">Silver Star</a></i>. Jacksonville was also served by the thrice-weekly <i><a href="/wiki/Sunset_Limited" title="Sunset Limited">Sunset Limited</a></i> and the daily <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silver_Palm_(Amtrak)" title="Silver Palm (Amtrak)">Silver Palm</a></i>. Service on the <i>Silver Palm</i> was cut back to <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah, Georgia</a> in 2002. The <i>Sunset Limited</i> route was truncated at <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio" title="San Antonio">San Antonio, Texas</a> as a result of the track damage in the Gulf Coast area caused by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> on August 28, 2005. Service was restored as far east as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans,_Louisiana" title="New Orleans, Louisiana">New Orleans</a> by late October 2005, but Amtrak has opted not to fully restore service into Florida.</p>
<p>Jacksonville is the headquarters of two significant freight railroads. <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">CSX Transportation</a>, owns a large building on the downtown riverbank that is a significant part of the skyline. <a href="/wiki/Florida_East_Coast_Railway" title="Florida East Coast Railway">Florida East Coast Railway</a> also calls Jacksonville home.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Aviation_Authority" title="Jacksonville Aviation Authority">Jacksonville Aviation Authority</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jacksonville_Int%27l.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Jacksonville_Int%27l.JPG/220px-Jacksonville_Int%27l.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Jacksonville_Int%27l.JPG/330px-Jacksonville_Int%27l.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Jacksonville_Int%27l.JPG/440px-Jacksonville_Int%27l.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jacksonville_Int%27l.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_International_Airport" title="Jacksonville International Airport">Jacksonville International Airport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Jacksonville is served by <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_International_Airport" title="Jacksonville International Airport">Jacksonville International Airport</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA</a>: <b>JAX</b>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>KJAX</b>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">LID</a>: <b>JAX</b>), 13 miles north of downtown, with 82 departures a day to 27 nonstop destination cities. Airports in Jacksonville are managed by the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Aviation_Authority" title="Jacksonville Aviation Authority">Jacksonville Aviation Authority</a> (JAA). Smaller aircraft use <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Executive_at_Craig_Airport" title="Jacksonville Executive at Craig Airport">Jacksonville Executive at Craig Airport</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA</a>: <b>CRG</b>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>KCRG</b>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">LID</a>: <b>CRG</b>) in Arlington, <a href="/wiki/Herlong_Recreational_Airport" title="Herlong Recreational Airport">Herlong Recreational Airport</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>KHEG</b>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">LID</a>: <b>HEG</b>) on the Westside, and <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Airport" title="Cecil Airport">Cecil Airport</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA</a>: <b>VQQ</b>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>KVQQ</b>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">LID</a>: <b>VQQ</b>), at <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Commerce_Center" title="Cecil Commerce Center">Cecil Commerce Center</a>. The state of Florida has designated Cecil Airport a space port, allowing horizontal lift spacecraft to use the facility.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Seaports">Seaports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Seaports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Port_Authority" title="Jacksonville Port Authority">Jacksonville Port Authority</a></div>
<p>Public seaports in Jacksonville are managed by the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Port_Authority" title="Jacksonville Port Authority">Jacksonville Port Authority</a>, known as <b>JAXPORT</b>. Four modern deepwater (40 ft) seaport facilities, including America's newest cruise port, make Jacksonville a full-service international seaport. In FY2006, JAXPORT handled 8.7 million tons of cargo, including nearly 610,000 vehicles, which ranks Jacksonville 2nd in the nation in automobile handling, behind only the <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port Authority of New York and New Jersey">Port Authority of New York and New Jersey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 20 other maritime facilities not managed by the Port Authority move about 10 million tons of additional cargo in and out of the St. Johns River. In terms of total tonnage, the Port of Jacksonville ranks 40th nationally; within Florida, it is 3rd behind Tampa and Port Everglades.</p>
<p>In 2003, the <a href="/wiki/JAXPORT_Cruise_Terminal" title="JAXPORT Cruise Terminal">JAXPORT Cruise Terminal</a> opened, providing cruise service for 1,500 passengers to <a href="/wiki/Key_West,_Florida" title="Key West, Florida">Key West, Florida</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carnival_Cruise_Lines" title="Carnival Cruise Lines">Carnival Cruise Lines</a> ship, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Celebration" title="Grand Celebration">Celebration</a>, which was retired in April 2008. For almost five months, no cruises originated from Jacksonville until September 20, 2008, when the cruise ship <a href="/wiki/Carnival_Fascination" title="Carnival Fascination">Fascination</a> departed with 2,079 passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup> In Fiscal year 2006, there were 78 cruise ship sailings with 128,745 passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup> A JaxPort spokesperson said in 2008 that they expect 170,000 passengers to sail each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Fire_and_Rescue" title="Jacksonville Fire and Rescue">Jacksonville Fire and Rescue</a> operates <a href="/wiki/Fireboats_of_Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Fireboats of Jacksonville, Florida">a fleet of three fireboats</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MenOfValorJacksonville_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-MenOfValorJacksonville-201">[199]</a></sup> Its vessels are called on to fight approximately 75 fires per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FemaFireboatsThenAndNow_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-FemaFireboatsThenAndNow-202">[200]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mayport_Ferry" title="Mayport Ferry">Mayport Ferry</a> connects the north and south ends of State Road A1A between Mayport and Fort George Island, and is the last active ferry in Florida. The state of Florida transferred responsibility for ferry operations to JAXPORT on October 1, 2007.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Electric_Authority" title="Jacksonville Electric Authority">Jacksonville Electric Authority</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JEANorthPP2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/JEANorthPP2011.jpg/220px-JEANorthPP2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/JEANorthPP2011.jpg/330px-JEANorthPP2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/JEANorthPP2011.jpg/440px-JEANorthPP2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JEANorthPP2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/JEA_Northside_Generating_Station" title="JEA Northside Generating Station">JEA Northside Generating Station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Basic utilities in Jacksonville (water, sewer, electric) are provided by <a href="/wiki/JEA" title="JEA">JEA</a> (formerly the Jacksonville Electric Authority). According to Article 21 of the <i>Jacksonville City Charter</i>,</p>
<blockquote>
<p>JEA is authorized to own, manage and operate a utilities system within and outside the City of Jacksonville. JEA is created for the express purpose of acquiring, constructing, operating, financing and otherwise have plenary authority with respect to electric, water, sewer, natural gas and such other utility systems as may be under its control now or in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[201]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/TECO_Energy" title="TECO Energy">People's Gas</a> is Jacksonville's natural gas provider. <a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a> is Jacksonville's local cable provider. <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Corporation" title="AT&amp;T Corporation">AT&amp;T</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/BellSouth" title="BellSouth">BellSouth</a>) is Jacksonville's local phone provider, and their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U-Verse" title="U-Verse">U-Verse</a> service offers TV, internet, and VoIP phone service to customers served by fiber-to-the-premises or fiber-to-the-node using a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_ready_access_device" title="Video ready access device">VRAD</a>. The city has a successful <a href="/wiki/Recycling" title="Recycling">recycling</a> program with separate pickups for garbage, <a href="/wiki/Green_waste" title="Green waste">yard waste</a> and recycling. Collection is provided by several private companies under contract to the City of Jacksonville.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Florida" title="List of hospitals in Florida">List of hospitals in Florida</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LifeFlight_Helicopter_Landing_Pad_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/LifeFlight_Helicopter_Landing_Pad_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-LifeFlight_Helicopter_Landing_Pad_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/LifeFlight_Helicopter_Landing_Pad_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-LifeFlight_Helicopter_Landing_Pad_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/LifeFlight_Helicopter_Landing_Pad_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-LifeFlight_Helicopter_Landing_Pad_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LifeFlight_Helicopter_Landing_Pad_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Landing pad at Baptist Medical Center Downtown</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Major players in the Jacksonville health care industry include <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent%27s_HealthCare" title="St. Vincent's HealthCare">St. Vincent's HealthCare</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist_Health_(Florida)" title="Baptist Health (Florida)">Baptist Health</a> and <a href="/wiki/UF_Health_Jacksonville" title="UF Health Jacksonville">UF Health Jacksonville</a> for local residents. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Nemours_Foundation" title="Nemours Foundation">Nemours Children's Clinic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mayo_Clinic_Jacksonville" title="Mayo Clinic Jacksonville">Mayo Clinic Jacksonville</a> each draw patients regionally.</p>
<p>The TaxExemptWorld.com website, which compiles <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">Internal Revenue Service</a> data, reported that in 2007, there are 2,910 distinct, active, tax exempt/non-profit organizations in Jacksonville which, excluding Credit Unions, had a total income of $7.08 billion and assets of $9.54 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup> There are 333 charitable organizations with assets of over $1 million. The largest share of assets was tied to Medical facilities, $4.5 billion. The problems of the homeless are addressed by several non-profits, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Sulzbacher_Center" title="Sulzbacher Center">Sulzbacher Center</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Clara_White_Mission" title="Clara White Mission">Clara White Mission</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Jacksonville,_Florida" title="List of people from Jacksonville, Florida">List of people from Jacksonville, Florida</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacksonville,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_sister_cities_in_Florida" title="List of sister cities in Florida">List of sister cities in Florida</a></div>
<p>Jacksonville has eight <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sister_cities" title="Sister cities">sister cities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[203]</a></sup> They are:</p>
<table>
<tr>
<td valign="top">
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina"><img alt="Argentina" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="800" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/23px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/35px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/46px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> - <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%ADa_Blanca" title="Bahía Blanca">Bahía Blanca</a>, Argentina (since 1967)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia"><img alt="Russia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> - <a href="/wiki/Murmansk" title="Murmansk">Murmansk</a>, Russia (1975)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea"><img alt="South Korea" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/45px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> - <a href="/wiki/Changwon" title="Changwon">Changwon</a>, South Korea (1983)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> - <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loire-Atlantique" title="Loire-Atlantique">Loire-Atlantique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pays_de_la_Loire" title="Pays de la Loire">Pays de la Loire</a>, France (1984)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/China" title="China"><img alt="China" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> - <a href="/wiki/Yingkou" title="Yingkou">Yingkou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liaoning" title="Liaoning">Liaoning</a>, China (1990)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa"><img alt="South Africa" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/45px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> - <a href="/wiki/Port_Elizabeth" title="Port Elizabeth">Port Elizabeth</a>/<a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_Bay_Metropolitan_Municipality" title="Nelson Mandela Bay Metropolitan Municipality">Nelson Mandela Bay</a>, South Africa (2000)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil"><img alt="Brazil" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="720" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/22px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/33px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/43px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 2x" width="22"/></a></span> - <a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">Curitiba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paraná (state)">Paraná</a>, Brazil (2009)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico"><img alt="Puerto Rico" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Flag_of_Puerto_Rico.svg/23px-Flag_of_Puerto_Rico.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Flag_of_Puerto_Rico.svg/35px-Flag_of_Puerto_Rico.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Flag_of_Puerto_Rico.svg/45px-Flag_of_Puerto_Rico.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> - <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a> (2009)</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<ul>
<li>In 2000, The <a href="/wiki/Sister_Cities_International" title="Sister Cities International">Sister Cities International</a> awarded Jacksonville the <i>Innovation Arts &amp; Culture Award</i> for the city's program with Nantes.</li>
</ul>

<li id="cite_note-71"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-71">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Mean monthly maxima and minima (i.e. the highest and lowest temperature readings during an entire month or year) calculated based on data at said location from 1981 to 2010.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-72">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Official records for Jacksonville were kept at downtown from September 1871 to December 1955, <a href="/wiki/Imeson_Field" title="Imeson Field">Imeson Field</a> from January 1, 1956 to January 18, 1971, and at Jacksonville Int'l since January 19, 1971. For more information, see <a class="external text" href="http://threadex.rcc-acis.org/" rel="nofollow">Threaded Station Extremes</a>.</span></li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">December 9,</span> 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJacksonville%2C+Florida&amp;rft.atitle=Men+of+Valor%3A+A+History+of+Firefighting+in+Jacksonville+Florida%2C+1886-1996&amp;rft.au=John+W.+Cowart&amp;rft.date=2006-03-01&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.isbn=9781411683006&amp;rft.pages=71%2C94-96%2C130&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DopQCI2XxDZgC%26pg%3DPA94%26dq%3Djacksonville%2Bfireboat%26hl%3Den%26sa%3DX%26ei%3DhUmmUtCFM8XGqgHd0oD4Dw%26redir_esc%3Dy%23v%3Donepage%26q%3Djacksonville%2520fireboat%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-FemaFireboatsThenAndNow-202"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FemaFireboatsThenAndNow_202-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">US Fire Administration. <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=sKNLPbi41A4C&amp;pg=PA23&amp;dq=jacksonville+fireboat&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ei=hUmmUtCFM8XGqgHd0oD4Dw&amp;redir_esc=y#v=onepage&amp;q=jacksonville%20fireboat&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow"><i>Special Report: Fireboats; Then and Now</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a>. p. 6,7,15,23<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">December 9,</span> 2013</span>. <q>One consistent feature of most fireboat training programs is the training for the fireboat captain or master. Often this individual is different than the officer assigned to coordinate fire attack. Though not required in all cases—mainly because fireboat vary in size—most fireboat captains are certified/licensed through the United States Coast Guard for operations of a vessel up to 100 tons. In some jurisdictions, such as Jacksonville, Florida, all crew members are required to be USCG-licensed regardless of what position they are assigned on the boat.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJacksonville%2C+Florida&amp;rft.au=US+Fire+Administration&amp;rft.btitle=Special+Report%3A+Fireboats%3B+Then+and+Now&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pages=6%2C7%2C15%2C23&amp;rft.pub=Federal+Emergency+Management+Agency&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DsKNLPbi41A4C%26pg%3DPA23%26dq%3Djacksonville%2Bfireboat%26hl%3Den%26sa%3DX%26ei%3DhUmmUtCFM8XGqgHd0oD4Dw%26redir_esc%3Dy%23v%3Donepage%26q%3Djacksonville%2520fireboat%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-203"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-203">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://library.municode.com/HTML/12174/level3/CHRELA_PTACHLACHJAFL_ART21JE.html" rel="nofollow">"Article 21. -JEA"</a> Municode website, Jacksonville City Charter</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-204"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-204">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.taxexemptworld.com/search.asp?pg=91&amp;type=os&amp;criteria=FL&amp;rc=4198&amp;ra=&amp;ri=&amp;re=&amp;prevpage=90&amp;city=Jacksonville" rel="nofollow">"Nonprofit Organization &amp; 501C3 Lookup by City - TaxExemptWorld"</a>. <i>www.taxexemptworld.com</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJacksonville%2C+Florida&amp;rft.atitle=Nonprofit+Organization+%26+501C3+Lookup+by+City+-+TaxExemptWorld&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=www.taxexemptworld.com&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.taxexemptworld.com%2Fsearch.asp%3Fpg%3D91%26type%3Dos%26criteria%3DFL%26rc%3D4198%26ra%3D%26ri%3D%26re%3D%26prevpage%3D90%26city%3DJacksonville&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-205"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-205">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.jsca.org" rel="nofollow">"Jacksonville Sisters Cities Association"</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">July 19,</span> 2007</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJacksonville%2C+Florida&amp;rft.btitle=Jacksonville+Sisters+Cities+Association&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.jsca.org&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<ul>
<li>Bartley, Abel A., and Jon L. Wakelyn<i>Keeping the Faith: Race, Politics, and Social Development in Jacksonville, Florida, 1940–1970,</i> Greenwood Publishing, 2000.</li>
<li>Cassanello, Robert. <i>To Render Invisible: Jim Crow and Public Life in New South Jacksonville.</i> Gainesville, FL: University Press of Florida, 2013.</li>
<li>Cowart, John Wilson. <i>Crackers and Carpetbaggers: Moments in the History of Jacksonville, Florida.</i></li>
<li>Cowart, John Wilson. <i>Heroes all: a history of firefighting in Jacksonville.</i></li>
<li>Crooks, James B. <i>Jacksonville: The Consolidation Story, from Civil Rights to the Jaguars,</i> University Press of Florida, 2004.</li>
<li>Foley, Bill; Wood, Wayne (2001). <i>The great fire of 1901</i> (1st ed.). Jacksonville, Florida: The Jacksonville Historical Society.</li>
<li>Jackson, David H., Jr., "'Industrious, Thrifty, and Ambitious': Jacksonville's African American Businesspeople during the Jim Crow Era," <i>Florida Historical Quarterly,</i> 90 (Spring 2012), 453–87.</li>
<li>Mason, Jr., Herman. <i>African-American Life in Jacksonville,</i> Arcadia Publishing, 1997.</li>
<li>Oehser, John. <i>Jags to Riches: The Cinderella Season of the Jacksonville Jaguars,</i> St. Martins Press, 1997.</li>
<li>Schaefer, Daniel. <i>From scratch pads and dreams: A ten year history of the University of North Florida,</i> University of North Florida, 1982.</li>
<li>Wagman, Jules. <i>Jacksonville and Florida's First Coast,</i> Windsor Publishing, 1989.</li>
<li>Williams, Caroyln. <i>Historic Photos of Jacksonville,</i> Turner Publishing Company, 2006.</li>
</ul>
